        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1455313970">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8219892201083142623">I picked up Linda Greenlaw's <a title="The Lobster Chronicles Life on a Very Small Island by Linda Greenlaw" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/173166.The_Lobster_Chronicles_Life_on_a_Very_Small_Island">The Lobster Chronicles: Life on a Very Small Island</a> while on Cape Cod this past weekend, and not wanting to leave the world of the New England fisherman, I dug out my copy of <em>The Perfect Storm</em> that I had picked up somewhere along the way because it happens to be one of my husband's all-time favorite movies.<br /><br />While I found this book fascinating, and a very accurate representation of what could have happened to the <em>Andrea Gail</em>, there were times that I felt that it got a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8219892201083142623">I picked up Linda Greenlaw's <a title="The Lobster Chronicles Life on a Very Small Island by Linda Greenlaw" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/173166.The_Lobster_Chronicles_Life_on_a_Very_Small_Island">The Lobster Chronicles: Life on a Very Small Island</a> while on Cape Cod this past weekend, and not wanting to leave the world of the New England fisherman, I dug out my copy of <em>The Perfect Storm</em> that I had picked up somewhere along the way because it happens to be one of my husband's all-time favorite movies.<br /><br />While I found this book fascinating, and a very accurate representation of what could have happened to the <em>Andrea Gail</em>, there were times that I felt that it got a little too technical. Also frequently Junger used terms that I had never heard of, but are probably very familiar to a fisherman or to a meteorologist. I also feel that Junger tried to be as respectful as possible to the victims and their families; he could easily have made this account far more lurid and dramatic just for the sake of making big bucks. Instead he sticks to the facts as much as possible, and to the most realistic occurrences for the doomed ship.<br /><br />I look forward to watching the movie, as I think perhaps this is one of the few books that might do better on the big screen. Regardless, I'd recommend this to anyone looking to learn more about huge storms and shipwrecks.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12864293132151287671">Narración periodística de una <em>tormentaca</em> que se formó frente a las costas de Nueva Inglaterra y Canadá y que absorbió los restos de un huracán tropical, convirtiéndose durante unos días en otro huracán en sí misma.     <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_89989675">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89989675" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1892060-cc" class="left imgcol" title="CC"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="CC" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/89989675?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 17, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1892060-cc" class="user" title="CC">CC</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/108229.The_Perfect_Storm" title="Hardcover 9780393050325" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer89989675">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12721713652647633323">We enter the doomed fate of the fishing boat, the Andrea Gail, mostly through the eyes of one of its six crew members, Bobby Shatford. Bobby's fiance, a divorced woman with three kids to supposrt -- Christina Cotter -- is depending on Bobby. In turn, Bobby, who owes thousands of dollars of back child support for his own two kids, is depending on his fishing time on the Andrea Gail. With the money made there they can pay off debts and start their new life together fresh. <br /><br />The Crow's Nest bar in Gl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12721713652647633323">We enter the doomed fate of the fishing boat, the Andrea Gail, mostly through the eyes of one of its six crew members, Bobby Shatford. Bobby's fiance, a divorced woman with three kids to supposrt -- Christina Cotter -- is depending on Bobby. In turn, Bobby, who owes thousands of dollars of back child support for his own two kids, is depending on his fishing time on the Andrea Gail. With the money made there they can pay off debts and start their new life together fresh. <br /><br />The Crow's Nest bar in Gloucester, Mass almost serves as a character on its own, and its beaten-down-but-surviving demeanor seems to be a metaphor for the men themselves. It comforts them after a trip with little money made, and celebrates with them when they arrive back in the harbor with thousands upon thousands in profit. <br /><br />This is a fishing town, and those in it live at the sea's cruel mercy. Of its provision. And of its wrath.<br /><br />It's in these descriptions -- of the bar, the men and their commraderie (or lack thereof) and the weary women that love them -- that the book came alive. Yet, dispersed throughout (I'd say two-thirds of the book total) involved endless passages on the history of fishing, the terminology of the boats, the rules of sea, and the psychology of storms and tracking them, and made the narrative flow faulter. I kept wanting to get back to Bobby and Christina, and Billy Tyne (the captain).<br /><br />With no background in anything involving the sea or fishing, I found the information and terminology difficult to hack through and ended up skipping pages at a time. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12721713652647633323">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_288281606">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/288281606" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2540655-roger" class="left imgcol" title="Roger"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1304939437p2/2540655.jpg" alt="Roger" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/288281606?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 04, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2540655-roger" class="user" title="Roger">Roger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/108229.The_Perfect_Storm" title="Hardcover 9780393050325" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2540655-roger?shelf=historical-non-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-non-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2540655-roger?shelf=sailing" class="actionLinkLite">sailing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer288281606">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16767322048971857706">A compelling read. The true tale of the long-line swordfish vessel Andrea Gail and her crew of seven out of Gloucester, Massachusetts who were lost to perhaps the most vicious storm the elements of the north Atlantic have generated in recorded history.<br /><br />Sebastian Junger interweaves the account with know facts of the crews encounter with the raging storm, necessary and well reasoned speculation to fill the gaps, along with a very accessible explanation of the dynamic natural forces that combined to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16767322048971857706">A compelling read. The true tale of the long-line swordfish vessel Andrea Gail and her crew of seven out of Gloucester, Massachusetts who were lost to perhaps the most vicious storm the elements of the north Atlantic have generated in recorded history.<br /><br />Sebastian Junger interweaves the account with know facts of the crews encounter with the raging storm, necessary and well reasoned speculation to fill the gaps, along with a very accessible explanation of the dynamic natural forces that combined to generate monstrous seas of up to 100 feet in height, and the seamanship tactics captain Billy Tyne would have employed in a desperate struggle to survive. <br /><br />I read this book while on vacation in the neighboring town of Rockport and finished it just as the movie of the same title was released in June of 2000. This made it possible to visit many of the places in Gloucester that Sebastian Junger describes in the book as I read it. The Crow's Nest bar and Cape Pond Ice, the fishing fleet at the docks and the smell of the sea. <br /><br />What I can tell from that is that is - Sebastian Junger has a talent for bringing his compelling subjects to life with an accuracy that will give you a true sense of place and events from the security of your own safe harbor. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16767322048971857706">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_292835763">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292835763" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6381073-jason-taylor" class="left imgcol" title="Jason Taylor"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1323925404p2/6381073.jpg" alt="Jason Taylor" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/292835763?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 11, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6381073-jason-taylor" class="user" title="Jason Taylor">Jason Taylor</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/108229.The_Perfect_Storm" title="Hardcover 9780393050325" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer292835763">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3356091277758013757">I really liked this book. It's a book that will have you in suspense the entire time you're reading it! It is also very dramatically sad and eventful, though. The crew of the Andrea Gail goes out to sea on the Atlantic Ocean for a fishing trip, look for some beautiful Sword Fish. This was an actually job, not just a bunch of buddies going out on a fishing trip for a couple of days. This was a real crew who went out for weeks and weeks at a time. And, to make it even more "fishy", it is written a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3356091277758013757">I really liked this book. It's a book that will have you in suspense the entire time you're reading it! It is also very dramatically sad and eventful, though. The crew of the Andrea Gail goes out to sea on the Atlantic Ocean for a fishing trip, look for some beautiful Sword Fish. This was an actually job, not just a bunch of buddies going out on a fishing trip for a couple of days. This was a real crew who went out for weeks and weeks at a time. And, to make it even more "fishy", it is written about a true tale! The Andrea Gail just arrives home after a long voyage/fight on the Atlantic. They spend the night with their loved ones. But, the time spent home is less of a stay than they attend to. They only stay for ONE night before they set sail again! They kiss their wives, girlfriends, and or kids, and brave up for another trip. The first couple days of the trip are going more than crappy. But then, they swing over for a spot that other fisherman have said is just infested with Marlin. BUT much like everything in this life, there is a catch. There is a strom brewing over there where two hurricanes are predicited to mash together. They decide to take the risk, not thinking it was a big one, and go and catch them selves some money! They spend a few days over there and catch more than what they had planned for! But then a tradgedy strikes... Their icing system where they store the fish breaks down... They have two decisions that they are forced to choose from. Sit out on the ocean and wait for that storm to pass over and let there catch all rot and be under a couple thousand bucks, or try and fight out the storms and come back living phat. Unfortunately, due to modern day society's cocky, greedy people that live in it, they decide to take the risk. At first everything's going great, but then they just keep on getting pounded in the storms. At last, when things can't get much worse, the boat starts taking on water, and eventually gets capsized by a gigantic title wave! What was supposed to be a nice payday, turned into living hell. And since this awful event, none of the members of the Andrea Gail have been seen since...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3356091277758013757">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_152284525">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152284525" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2034676-gossymotto" class="left imgcol" title="Gossymotto"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Gossymotto" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/152284525?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2034676-gossymotto" class="user" title="Gossymotto">Gossymotto</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/108229.The_Perfect_Storm" title="Hardcover 9780393050325" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2034676-gossymotto?shelf=non-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2034676-gossymotto?shelf=nautical-disaster" class="actionLinkLite">nautical-disaster</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2034676-gossymotto?shelf=human-endurance" class="actionLinkLite">human-endurance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152284525">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12891141791648504111">I enjoyed the movie (George Clooney, Mark Wahlberg, Diane Lane), and found it to be an incredible story, but like most true stories, if you want more of the fact you have to read the book.<br /><br />Sebastian Junger does an excellent job of telling this story and since nobody knows for sure, what happened in the last moments on the Andrea Gail, he fills this in with the best possible information, by interviewing others that have faced similar conditions so that in reading it, you understand just what the c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12891141791648504111">I enjoyed the movie (George Clooney, Mark Wahlberg, Diane Lane), and found it to be an incredible story, but like most true stories, if you want more of the fact you have to read the book.<br /><br />Sebastian Junger does an excellent job of telling this story and since nobody knows for sure, what happened in the last moments on the Andrea Gail, he fills this in with the best possible information, by interviewing others that have faced similar conditions so that in reading it, you understand just what the crew would have been doing in an attempt to stay afloat and get back safely. It doesn't really matter which day or which wave it was that finally did them in because, as Junger describes it, there options would have just kept disappearing one after the other until there was nothing left that they could do. Out of all the things that could have happened in the end, he details them all and then draws reasonable conclusion to what would have most likely been the final moment but you have all the scenarios to think through yourself as the reader.<br /><br />What you really find here though is a sense of the desperation and the severity of the situation, and just how bad their luck turned out to be (or how lucky the rest of the fleet was). Junger also provides plenty of information on how ocean currents flow, the effect of temperature, sustained wind, and the skill it takes to navigate the north Atlantic. He also give chilling details of what the process of drowning is and what a person will go through (physically and mentally) as their life is ending.<br /><br />This story is haunting and sad. It will stay with you for a long time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12891141791648504111">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8Fd9qfMbezYIP/QRD/Y9Z7PRcCm0OTjdyGyvt2ErDk2Vg0J6AclvzITngKpxl9vV+iazMP3kf3eiZaolrb74CA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uk7Gqd0pUxWIDuUvYYX90W2+n/h+S9R9gmMqQcp+fCDfmvl6L/tH7wTWkZQf5BtjJElc4TeWk9foai/TBuuKZQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

Weaving a treacherous path through the freezing Weddell Sea, they had come within eighty-five miles of their destination when their ship, Endurance, was trapped fast in the ice pack. Soon the ship was crushed like matchwood, leaving the crew stranded on the floes. Their ordeal would last for twenty months, and they would make two near-fatal attempts to escape by open boat before their final rescue.Drawing upon previously unavailable sources, Caroline Alexander gives us a riveting account of Shackleton\'s expedition--one of history\'s greatest epics of survival. And she presents the astonishing work of Frank Hurley, the Australian photographer whose visual record of the adventure has never before been published comprehensively. Together, text and image re-create the terrible beauty of Antarctica, the awful destruction of the ship, and the crew\'s heroic daily struggle to stay alive, a miracle achieved largely through Shackleton\'s inspiring leadership. The survival of Hurley\'s remarkable images is scarcely less miraculous: The original glass plate negatives, from which most of the book\'s illustrations are superbly reproduced, were stored in hermetically sealed cannisters that survived months on the ice floes, a week in an open boat on the polar seas, and several more months buried in the snows of a rocky outcrop called Elephant Island. Finally Hurley was forced to abandon his professional equipment; he captured some of the most unforgettable images of the struggle with a pocket camera and three rolls of Kodak film.Published in conjunction with the American Museum of Natural History\'s landmark exhibition on Shackleton\'s journey, The Endurance thrillingly recounts one of the last great adventures in the Heroic Age of exploration--perhaps the greatest of them all.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"8194756998722758663\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent($(this));; return false;\"&gt;...more&lt;\/a&gt;\n\n Expedition leader Arlene Blum here tells their dramatic story: the logistical problems, storms, and hazardous ice climbing; the conflicts and reconciliations within the team; the terror of avalanches that threatened to sweep away camps and climbers.On October 15, two women and two Sherpas at last stood on the summit—but the celebration was cut short, for two days later, the two women of the second summit team fell to their deaths.Never before has such an account of mountaineering triumph and tragedy been told from a woman’s point of view. By proving that women had the skill, strength, and courage necessary to make this difficult and dangerous climb, the 1978 Women\'s Himalayan Expedition’s accomplishment had a positive impact around the world, changing perceptions about women’s abilities in sports and other arenas. And Annapurna: A Woman’s Place has become an acknowledged classic in the annals of women’s achievements—a story of challenge and commitment told with passion, humor, and unflinching <script>
//&lt;![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_30044'), "\n\n  &lt;h2&gt;&lt;a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"http://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30044.Young_Men_and_Fire?from_choice=false&amp;amp;from_home_module=false\"&gt;Young Men and Fire&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;\/h2&gt;\n\n      &lt;div&gt;\n        by &lt;a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/16943.Norman_Maclean?a=7&amp;amp;origin=related_works\"&gt;Norman Maclean&lt;\/a&gt;\n      &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n          &lt;div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\"&gt;\n            &lt;span class=\"minirating\"&gt;&lt;span class=\"stars staticStars\"&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;\/span&gt; 4.07 avg rating &amp;mdash; 3,122 ratings&lt;\/span&gt;            &amp;mdash; published 1992\n          &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n    &lt;div class=\"addBookTipDescription\"&gt;\n      \n&lt;span id=\"freeTextContainer10591930867679077108\"&gt;  On August 5, 1949, a crew of fifteen of the United States Forest Service\'s elite airborne firefighters, The Smoke Jumpers, stepped into the sky above a remote forest fire in the Montana wilderness. Two hours after their jump, all but three of these&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText10591930867679077108\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;     On August 5, 1949, a crew of fifteen of the United States Forest Service\'s elite airborne firefighters, The Smoke Jumpers, stepped into the sky above a remote forest fire in the Montana wilderness. Two hours after their jump, all but three of these men were dead or mortally burned from a &amp;quot;blowup&amp;quot; -- an explosive, 2,000-degree firestorm 300 feet deep and 200 feet tall -- a deadly explosion of flame and wind rarely encountered and little understood at the time.  Only seconds ahead of the approaching firestorm, the foreman, R. Wagner Dodge, throws himself into the ashes of an &amp;quot;escape fire &amp;quot; - and survives as most of his confused men run, their last moments obscured by smoke. The parents of the dead cry murder, charging that the foreman\'s fire killed their boys.  Exactly what happened in Mann Gulch that day has been obscured by years of grief and controversy. Now a master storyteller finally gives the Mann Gulch fire its due as tragedy.\n     These first deaths among the Forest Service\'s elite firefighters prompted widespread examination of federal fire policy, of the field of fire science, and of the frailty of young men. For Maclean, who witnessed the fire from the ground in August of 1949,  and even then he knew he would one day become a part of its story.  It is a story of Montana, of the ways of wildfires, firefighters, and fire scientists, and especially of a crew, young and proud, who &amp;quot;hadn\'t learned to count the odds and to sense they might owe the universe a tragedy.&amp;quot; This tale is also Maclean\'s own, the story of a writer obsessed by a strange and human horror, unable to let the truth die with these young men, searching for the last - and lasting - word. A canvas on which to tell many stories, including the story of his research into the story itself. And finally Nature\'s violence colliding with human fallibility.\n      Haunted by these deaths for forty years, Norman Maclean returned to the scene with two of the survivors and pursues the mysteries that Mann Gulch has kept hidden since 1949.  From the words of witnesses, the evidence of history, and the research of fire scientists, Maclean at last assembles the scattered pieces of the Mann Gulch tragedy; in his last work that consumed 14 years of his life, and earned a 1992 National Book Critics Circle Award.\n       The excruciating detail of this book makes for a sobering reading experience. Maclean -- a former University of Chicago English professor and avid fisherman -- also wrote \n  A River Runs Through It and Other Stories\n, which is set along the Missouri River, one gulch downstream from Mann Gulch.\n\n       &amp;quot;A magnificent drama of writing, a tragedy that pays tribute to the dead and offers rescue to the living.... Maclean\'s search for the truth, which becomes an exploration of his own mortality, is more compelling even than his journey into the heart of the fire. His description of the conflagration terrifies, but it is his battle with words, his effort to turn the story of the 13 men into tragedy that makes this book a classic.&amp;quot; \n         —  from New York Times Book Review Editor\'s Choice, Best Books of 1992\n\n\n  The Men who Perished in the Mann Gulch Fire:\n\nRobert J. Bennett&amp;#x2028;\nEldon E. Diettert&amp;#x2028;\nJames O. Harrison\n&amp;#x2028;William J. Heilman&amp;#x2028;\nPhillip R. McVey&amp;#x2028;\nDavid R. Navon&amp;#x2028;\nLeonard L. Piper&amp;#x2028;\nStanley J. Reba&amp;#x2028;\nMarvin L. Sherman&amp;#x2028;\nJoseph B. Sylvia\n&amp;#x2028;Henry J. Thol, Jr.\n&amp;#x2028;Newton R. Thompson\n&amp;#x2028;Silas R. Thompson\n\n\n  Survivors of the Fire:\n\nR. Wagner Dodge, foreman&amp;#x2028;\nWalter B. Rumsey\n&amp;#x2028;Robert W. First published in 1931, Endurance tells the full story of that doomed 1914-16 expedition and incredible rescue, as well as relating Worsley\'s further adventures fighting U-boats in the Great War, sailing the equally treacherous waters of the Arctic, and making one final (and successful) assault on the South Pole with Shackleton. It is a tale of unrelenting high adventure and a tribute to one of the most inspiring and courageous leaders of men in the history of exploration.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16494.Sebastian_Junger">About Sebastian Junger</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/16494.Sebastian_Junger"><img alt="16494" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1272350217p2/16494.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7043166193477128823">Sebastian Junger is an American author and journalist. He graduated from Concord Academy in 1980 and received a Bachelor of Arts degree from Wesleyan University in cultural anthropology in 1984. He received a National Magazine Award in 2000 for "The Forensics of War," published in Vanity Fair in 1999. In 1997, with the publication of his work, The Perfect Storm, he was touted as the new Hemingway,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7043166193477128823">Sebastian Junger is an American author and journalist. He graduated from Concord Academy in 1980 and received a Bachelor of Arts degree from Wesleyan University in cultural anthropology in 1984. He received a National Magazine Award in 2000 for "The Forensics of War," published in Vanity Fair in 1999. In 1997, with the publication of his work, The Perfect Storm, he was touted as the new Hemingway, and helped usher a renewed interest in adventure non-fiction.<br />-Wikipedia<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7043166193477128823">...more</a>

    </div>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/list/16494.Sebastian_Junger">Books by Sebastian Junger</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
    <div data-current-user-id="false" data-use-wtr-tooltip="true" class="js-dataTooltip">
        <div data-placement="bottom-left" data-resource-id="7519640" data-resource-type="Book" class="js-tooltipTrigger tooltipTrigger">
          <a href="/book/show/7519640-war"><img width="50" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/books/1344271278m/7519640.jpg" id="more_book_7519640" /></a>
